(PCP) as advised.
Incision Care:
*Please call your doctor or nurse practitioner if you have 
increased pain, swelling, redness, or drainage from the incision 
site.
*Avoid swimming and baths until your follow-up appointment.
*You may shower, and wash surgical incisions with a mild soap 
and warm water.  Gently pat the area dry.
*If you have steri-strips, they will fall off on their own.  
Please remove any remaining strips ___ days after surgery.
.
G/J-tube: Keep capped. Monitor for signs and symptoms of 
infection or dislocation.

#AMS/ metabolic encephalopathy:

Etiology was presumed hypoactive delirium in setting of UTI. 
Despite adequate treatment and fluid resuscitation mental status 
worsened on first day of admission for unclear reasons; patient  
became progressively more somnolent with periods of apnea.

She was given 0.4 mg narcan with improvement, raising concern

drip patient was transferred to MICU.

Brief Hospital Course:
BRIEF SUMMARY STATEMENT:
===========================
Ms ___ is a ___ woman with a history of cadaveric renal 
transplant (on Prednisone & Tacrolimus), pAF, prior NSTEMI, HTN 
& chronic abdominal and back pain, who presented from her 
nursing home with fever, nausea, vomiting, & lethargy, 
concerning for sepsis. She was treated with IV antibiotics in 
the ICU initially(Daptomycin & Cefepime, followed by 
Vanc/Zosyn). Once stabilized, she was transferred to the floor. 

ACTIVE ISSUES:
===========================
# SEPSIS: 
Patient presented with fever, tachycardia, and altered mental 
status, concerning for sepsis. Given her immunosuppression, she 
was at high risk for infection. She denied urinary symptoms, and 
urine cx was negative, but she does have a history of VRE UTI. 
She had no cough, and CXR had no evidence of pneumonia. She 
denied headache or neck stiffness, and LP without evidence of 
meningitis. She does have a history of C diff, and is on 
treatment with oral Vancomycin; no recent diarrhea, but did 
present with abdominal pain. No skin lesions. Viral & tick-borne 
illness were tested and were negative. CT A/P ___ showed LLL 
changes c/w ? aspiration vs. PNA as well as debris in bladder. 
MRI spine ___ with stable L2-L3 intervertebral disc space fluid 
collection likely due to degenerative changes. UA She was 
treated initially with a dose of Daptomycin & Cefepime. This was 
transitioned to Vancomycin 750 mg IV Q 24H and 
Piperacillin-Tazobactam 4.5 g IV Q8H, which were stopped on 
___. She was continued on Vancomycin Oral Liquid ___ mg PO/NG 
Q6H for known C diff for 14d. She was also continued on home 
immunosuppression with Tacrolimus 0.5 mg PO Q12H and PredniSONE 
5 mg PO/NG DAILY.

# IATROGENIC HYPERTHYROIDISM: 
On admission, TSH was very low at 0.04 & T4 high at 2.5, 
concerning for hyperthyroidism. She has a history of 
hypothyroidism, diagnosed in ___, and had been on Synthroid 
since then. Per pharmacy records, she has been taking Synthroid 
___ daily since ___. T3 wnl and elevated free T4 concerning 
for iatrogenic hyperthyroid per endocrine team. Synthroid was 
decreased to 88mcg daily. 

# TOXIC METABOLIC ENCEPHALOPATHY: 
At baseline, patient is A&Ox3. During this hospitalization, her 
mental status waxed & waned, with more confusion in the morning. 
She was at high risk for delirium given her age, comorbidities, 
and ICU stay. Her mental status improved to baseline during her 
hospital stay. 

# ABDOMINAL PAIN: 
Patient reported chronic abdominal pain at baseline. Per recent 
admission, OSH EGD ___ was notable for grade II esophageal 
varices and gastric ulcer. Recent RUQ U/S with suspicion for 
cirrhosis. LFTs all negative & lactate remained normal. She has 
tolerated a regular diet. Abdominal exam remained benign. She 
was given Omeprazole, Maalox/Diphenhydramine/Lidocaine 15 mL PO 
TID:PRN abd pain and Sucralfate 1 gm PO/NG TID:PRN abdominal 
pain.

# ESRD S/P RENAL TRANSPLANT: 
Cr remained at baseline of 1.0-1.2 during admission. Renal 
transplant ultrasound was normal on admission. Continued home 
immunosuppression with Tacrolimus 0.5 mg PO Q12H and PredniSONE 
5 mg PO/NG DAILY & prophylaxis with Acyclovir 400 mg PO Q12H. 
Nephrology transplant was consulted, appreciate their recs.
